# Sri Navadvipa Panjika, Gaurabda 540
## English translation of the scanned edition - corrected working revision 2

**Source:** 57 PDF scans of the book. The first scan is the cover; the remaining scans contain two-page spreads.

**Accuracy note:** printed pages 2-20 were translated with manual inspection of the images. The calendar section was structured from enhanced OCR of the Bengali scans. All 385 civil dates are retained without omissions. The symbol **approximately** before a time means that a digit was reconstructed from a typical OCR substitution and the sequence of neighbouring dates. `[not recognised]` means that no reliable reading was obtained. Before practical use, exact tithi, nakshatra, parana and yoga times must be checked against the original scan.

**Revision 2 corrections:** the entries for 15-18 and 29-30 June 2026 were read again directly from the original Bengali scans. Incorrectly recognised month-day numbers, tithi boundaries and nakshatra boundaries were corrected. In particular, on 16 June Gaura Pratipada ends at 06:37, followed by Gaura Dvitiya until 04:13 the following night; on 29 June Purnima ends at 04:48; and on 30 June Krishna Pratipada and Purva Ashadha are printed as lasting throughout the day.

**Methodological limitation:** the source panjika publishes completed calendar times but does not disclose the exact astronomical model used to calculate the longitudes of the Sun and Moon. Its printed times cannot be reproduced by applying a constant correction to a modern geocentric ephemeris; the observed differences vary in magnitude.

---

# Scan 1 - Cover

**Introduced by Jagad-guru Prabhupada Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Goswami Thakur**

## SRI NAVADVIPA PANJIKA

**Sri Gaurabda 540**

Bengali Era: **1432-1433**  
Christian Era: **2026-2027**

Edited by **Sri Panagopala Brahmachari** *(শ্রীপাণগোপাল ব্রহ্মচারী; the reading of the name follows the scan)*.

All rights reserved by Mayapur Sri Chaitanya Math.

Issued by the principal Math, Sri Chaitanya Math, situated in Sridham Mayapur.

Approved by the former Acharya of Sri Chaitanya Math, **Srila Bhaktiprajnana Yati Goswami Maharaj**.

Published and printed by the Acharya and General Secretary of Sri Chaitanya Math, **Tridandi Swami Srimad Bhaktisvarupa Sannyasi Maharaj**.

Price: **30 taka**.

# Scan 2 - Printed page 2

## The Order of Sri Navadvipa Parikrama
### Written by Om Vishnupada Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur

The island formed by the meeting of the Ganga and Yamuna  
is called Antardvipa in all the sastras.

Within Antardvipa is the holy place Mayapur,  
where Lord Sri Chaitanya Thakur appeared.

Know, O devotees, that Mayapur in Navadvipa  
is Mahavana situated within Goloka.

Svetadvipa, Vaikuntha, Goloka and Vrindavana -  
all these tattvas are eternally present in Navadvipa.

Ayodhya, Mathura, Maya, Kasi, Kanchi,  
Avanti and Dvaraka - the essence of the seven holy cities -

all of them, each in its proper place,  
are eternally present in Navadvipa by the will of Gaurachandra.

Mayapur is the form of Maya bearing the Ganga;  
its greatness is abundantly praised in the sastras.  
*[This line is rendered literally; its grammatical analysis may require refinement.]*

One who comes to Mayapur even once  
easily crosses material maya.

When a person circumambulates Mayapur, the power of maya  
goes far away, and there is no further birth.

To the north of Mayapur lies Simantadvipa.  
This is the order of parikrama constantly taught in the sadhu-sastras.

After taking darsan of Antardvipa-Mayapur,  
O thoughtful devotees, proceed to Sri Simantadvipa.

The island called Godruma lies south of Mayapur.  
After circumambulating it, joyfully proceed to Madhyadvipa.

These four islands lie on the eastern bank of Jahnavi.  
After seeing them, cross Jahnavi without haste.

Having easily completed the circuit of Koladvipa,  
then behold the beauty of Ritudvipa.

After that comes beautiful Jahnudvipa.  
O best of the wise, then proceed to Modadrumadvipa.

Then cross the Ganga once more and see Rudradvipa.  
After circumambulating it, the devotees return again to Mayapur.

There, in the temple of Sri Jagannatha and Sachi,  
enter peacefully for the darsan of the Lord.

Such a parikrama may be performed at any time;  
it is an abode where the living being obtains unlimited happiness.

It is especially auspicious from the tithi of Makari Saptami  
until Phalguna Purnima, in an excellent assembly of devotees.

The mahajana who completes the parikrama  
and comes to Mayapur for darsan on the Appearance Day

receives the mercy of Nitai and Gauranga:  
They grant shelter at Their feet and eligibility for bhakti.

### Note in the book

Every year, according to the regulations of Sri Chaitanya Math in Sridham Mayapur, the nine islands of Sri Navadvipa are circumambulated in the order given above, accompanied by sankirtana and a festive procession. Thereafter the **Sri Navadvipa-dhama Pracharini Sabha** conducts a three-day Sri Sri Gaura-janmotsava festival at Sri Yogapitha.

---

# Scan 2 - Printed page 3

## Preface

The all-merciful Srila Jiva Goswami Prabhu composed the **Sri Harinamamrita-vyakarana** so that even while studying grammar one might receive an excellent opportunity to practise Sri Harinama. In the same way, the founder of Sri Chaitanya Math and its branches, the Sri Gaudiya Maths - the infinitely merciful Prabhupada Sri Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Goswami Thakur - introduced the **Sri Navadvipa Panjika**. By assigning various names of Vishnu to the months, paksas, weekdays and other calendar units, he provided a special opportunity to perform Sri Harinama-kirtana even while working with the calendar.

The vratas, fasts and other regulations in this panjika are presented according to pure Vaishnava siddhanta. Several important explanations follow.

### System of the year and months

The year of the Sri Navadvipa Panjika is a lunar year. It begins with Krishna Pratipada after Phalguna Purnima - the Purnima of the Appearance of Sri Gaura - and continues until the next Purnima of Sri Gaura's Appearance.

A month is counted from Krishna Pratipada through Purnima. The twelve months of Sri Gauranga bear the following names in order:

1. Vishnu;
2. Madhusudana;
3. Trivikrama;
4. Vamana;
5. Sridhara;
6. Hrishikesa;
7. Padmanabha;
8. Damodara;
9. Kesava;
10. Narayana;
11. Madhava;
12. Govinda.

Approximately every two years and eight months an additional month appears, called **Purushottama-masa**. The original prints that it continues "from Sukla Pratipada to Amavasya"; this wording is reproduced literally.

Smartas attached to karma and matter call this month **mala-masa** and refrain during it from all auspicious worldly rites. Pure Vaishnavas, by contrast, regard Sri Purushottama-masa as supremely sacred and spend it in uninterrupted service to Bhagavan.

### Names of the weekdays

- Sunday - **Sarva-Vasudeva**;
- Monday - **Sarva-Siva-Sankarsana**;
- Tuesday - **Sthanu-Pradyumna**;
- Wednesday - **Bhuta-Aniruddha**;
- Thursday - **Adi-Karanodakasayi**;
- Friday - **Nidhi-Garbhodakasayi**;
- Saturday - **Avyaya-Ksirodakasayi**.

### Names of the paksas

- Krishna-paksa - **Padmaja-Krishna** *(the first compound name is not fully certain in the scan)*;
- Sukla-paksa - **Aniruddha-Gaura**.

### Names of the tithis

- Pratipada - Brahma;
- Dvitiya - Sripati;
- Tritiya - Vishnu;
- Chaturthi - Kapila;
- Panchami - Sridhara;
- Shashthi - Prabhu;
- Saptami - Damodara;
- Ashtami - Hrishikesa;
- Navami - Govinda;
- Dashami - Madhusudana;
- Ekadashi - Bhudhara;
- Dvadashi - Gadi;
- Trayodashi - Sankhi;
- Chaturdashi - Padmi;
- Purnima or Amavasya - Chakri.

---

# Scan 3 - Printed page 4

## Names of the nakshatras

- Asvini - Dhata;
- Bharani - Krishna;
- Krittika - Visva;
- Rohini - Vishnu;
- Mrigasira - Vasatkara;
- Ardra - Bhuta-bhavya-bhavat-prabhu;
- Punarvasu - Bhuta-bhrit;
- Pushya - Bhuta-krit;
- Aslesa - Bhava;
- Magha - Bhutatma;
- Purva-phalguni - Bhuta-bhavana;
- Uttara-phalguni - Avyakta;
- Hasta - Pundarikaksa;
- Chitra - Visvakarma;
- Svati - Suchisrava;
- Visakha - Srasta;
- Anuradha - Bhavana;
- Jyestha - Bharta;
- Mula - Prabhava;
- Purva Ashadha - Prabhu;
- Uttara Ashadha - Isvara;
- Sravana - Aprameya;
- Dhanistha - Hrishikesa;
- Satabhisa - Padmanabha;
- Purva Bhadrapada - Amara-prabhu;
- Uttara Bhadrapada - Agrahya;
- Revati - Sasvata.

The book states that these names occur in the **Vishnudharmottara** and the **Hayasirsa-pancharatra**. It also calls Uttarayana **Balabhadra** and Daksinayana **Krishna**.

## Names of the seasons

- Vasanta - Madhava;
- Grishma - Pundarikaksa;
- Varsa - Bhogasayi;
- Sarad - Padmanabha;
- Hemanta - Hrishikesa;
- Sita - Deva-Trivikrama.

## Purpose of the panjika

On the one hand, this panjika is especially necessary for remembering and chanting Sri Harinama. On the other hand, it is indispensable for identifying fasting days, parvas and festivals according to the pure conclusions of the Vaishnava smrti **Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa**.

Fasting is prescribed on Ekadashi, Mahadvadashi and the appearance days of Vishnu-tattvas. When a Mahadvadashi occurs, the Ekadashi is set aside and the fast is observed specifically on Dvadashi.

If no Mahadvadashi occurs on the appearance day of a Vishnu-tattva, one should fast on Ekadashi, and on Dvadashi worship the corresponding Vishnu-vigraha, offer bhoga and perform parana. This rule is found in Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa and is explained especially clearly in the section on Sri Vamana-dvadashi. The present panjika follows the conclusions of Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa.

Gaudiya Vaishnavas, remembering the devotional mood associated with Sri Gaurasundara, Sri Baladeva Prabhu and Sri Nityananda Prabhu, observe a fast on the tithis of Their appearance. The corresponding rule is therefore included in this panjika.

## Consideration of viddha on fasting days

Viddha is of two kinds: **purva-viddha**, contamination by the preceding tithi, and **para-viddha**, contamination by the following tithi.

Purva-viddha is itself of two kinds: contamination at sunrise and contamination at midnight. Although consideration of midnight viddha is accepted in the Nimbarka sampradaya, the revered Srila Sanatana Goswami demonstrated in his commentary on Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa that there is no sound reason to accept it.

---

# Scan 3 - Printed page 5

Among the kinds of purva-viddha, Ekadashi, or Harivasara, is to be rejected when Arunodaya is touched by Dashami.

Here the word **Harivasara** means the Ekadashi fasting day. Because the first quarter of Dvadashi belongs to the period of the Ekadashi fast, it too is called Harivasara.

For all other tithis connected with appearances of Bhagavan and similar festivals, arunodaya-viddha is not rejected; only contamination by the preceding tithi at sunrise is rejected. This is the general rule for rejecting viddha.

Some inexperienced persons think that "rejecting viddha" always means rejecting arunodaya-viddha. This is entirely mistaken. To clarify the matter, the reasoning of Srila Sanatana Goswami from his commentary on Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa is presented.

### Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa 12.315 - meaning of the verse

> All tithis beginning with Pratipada are called complete when they extend from one sunrise to the next; Harivasara is the exception.

The marks of completeness and contamination are then explained. According to the Skanda Purana, Pratipada and the following tithis are called **complete** when they occupy sixty dandas, from one sunrise until the next.

For Ekadashi the rule is different: if Ekadashi begins at least one muhurta before sunrise, it is considered complete.

Therefore:

- for every tithi other than Ekadashi, if the preceding tithi is still present at sunrise, the current tithi is viddha;
- for Ekadashi, Arunodaya is considered - two muhurtas, or four dandas, approximately **1 hour 36 minutes before sunrise**;
- if Dashami is present at Arunodaya, Ekadashi is arunodaya-viddha, a form of purva-viddha.

### The following verse - meaning

> Nanda, meaning Ekadashi, is to be rejected as purva-viddha even when joined with the Sravana nakshatra. In the same way, a purva-viddha Ashtami is to be rejected even when joined with its auspicious nakshatra.

The book explains: just as Ekadashi, called Nanda, is rejected when purva-viddha even in conjunction with Sravana, so Janmashtami is to be rejected when purva-viddha even in conjunction with Rohini.

---

# Scan 4 - Printed page 6

In his commentary on this verse, Srila Sanatana Goswami clearly says that because of the word **"similarly"**, some think that just as Ekadashi is rejected when it touches Dashami at Arunodaya, Janmashtami should be rejected if Saptami remains at Arunodaya. That interpretation is incorrect.

The reason is that all tithis other than Ekadashi are complete if they have begun by sunrise. Their contact with the preceding tithi at Arunodaya therefore does not produce viddha. This follows from the preceding definition of a complete tithi.

It should be especially understood that a tithi free from actual viddha is complete. To attribute viddha to a complete tithi is merely a sign of misunderstanding.

The Gaudiya Vaishnava acharya Srila Baladeva Vidyabhusana writes directly in the ninth prameya of Prameya-ratnavali - meaning:

> Only for the Ekadashi fast is a tithi contaminated at Arunodaya to be rejected. Janmashtami and other vratas are to be rejected when they are contaminated by the preceding tithi at sunrise.

In other words, arunodaya-viddha is rejected only for the Sri Ekadashi vrata. For other vratas only suryodaya-viddha, contamination at sunrise, is rejected.

The founder of Sri Chaitanya Math and the Sri Gaudiya Maths, Prabhupada 108 Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Goswami Thakur, also wrote in his explanation of Sri Chaitanya-charitamrita, Madhya-lila 24.337, that arunodaya-viddha is to be rejected for Ekadashi, while suryodaya-viddha is to be rejected for other vratas, and only the pure vrata should be observed.

Some maintain that the Sri Janmashtami fast should be observed only on an Ashtami joined with Navami. The book calls this view mistaken.

Certainly an Ashtami contaminated by Saptami at sunrise is to be rejected, and the fast is observed on Ashtami joined with Navami. But if Saptami is no longer present at sunrise, the fast should be observed on that Ashtami day.

If Ashtami is extended and continues into the next day, parana is performed after Ashtami ends on the following day. Otherwise the previously stated parana rules would be impossible.

Ordinarily the fast is observed on a pure tithi after purva-viddha has been removed. There are, however, specific exceptions.

### 1. Sri Janmashtami

A verse from the Skanda Purana quoted in Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa 15.352 says in meaning:

> If a small portion of Ashtami remains at sunrise, after which Navami occupies the entire day and night, and the day is joined with Wednesday and Rohini, such a rare yoga may not occur even in a hundred years.

---

# Scan 4 - Printed page 7

The Skanda Purana continues: if only a small portion of Ashtami remains at sunrise, Navami then occupies the whole day and night, and Wednesday and Rohini are present, such a yoga is exceedingly rare.

The next verse, quoted in Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa 15.354, establishes the following rule in meaning.

Even if the preceding day is Monday or Wednesday, when a pure Ashtami is extended and on the following day is joined with Rohini, the fast is observed on the following day - the extended Ashtami joined with Navami.

If pure Ashtami is joined with Rohini on both the preceding and following days, one fasts on the day when Rohini is present at midnight.

If Rohini is present at midnight on both days, the fast is observed on the preceding day.

### Rule for parana after Janmashtami

The meanings of Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa 15.403-405 are given as follows:

> Parana should never be performed while either Ashtami or Rohini continues. Doing so destroys previously accumulated pious acts and the fruit of the fast.
>
> Violation of the tithi destroys the fruit eightfold, and violation of the nakshatra fourfold. Therefore parana should be carefully performed only after both the tithi and nakshatra have ended.
>
> Some Vaishnavas, moved by bhakti on the auspicious day of the great festival of Bhagavan's appearance, perform parana after the festival has concluded.

Therefore parana cannot be performed while Ashtami or Rohini remains. Otherwise the result of previous religious acts and of the fast is lost.

Parana must consequently be performed after both factors - tithi and nakshatra - have ended. Some exalted Vaishnavas perform it after the celebration of Bhagavan's appearance is complete.

---

# Scan 5 - Printed page 8

### 2. Sri Ramanavami

The Sri Ramanavami fast is to be observed on the pure Sukla Navami of the month of Chaitra.

However, if because of a ksaya tithi a pure Ekadashi follows the pure Navami on the next day, the fast is prescribed on the Navami contaminated by Ashtami. See the fourteenth vilasa of Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa.

### 3. Appearance of Sri Vamanadeva

The appearance tithi of Sri Vamanadeva is the Sukla Dvadashi of the month of Bhadra.

Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa nevertheless prescribes fasting on Ekadashi and performing parana on Dvadashi, after worshipping Sri Vamanadeva during the night of Ekadashi or at the beginning of Dvadashi. See the fifteenth vilasa of Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa.

## The day of Sri Govardhana Puja

Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa clearly states - meaning of the verse:

> This most excellent servant of Sri Krishna, Sri Govardhana Hill, is to be worshipped by Vaishnavas in the morning of Kartika Sukla Pratipada.

It then says: **"Thereafter Govardhana is to be worshipped in the morning."** Thus, according to Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa, the full Govardhana Puja is performed on the day whose morning is occupied by Kartika Sukla Pratipada.

If Pratipada is extended and continues on the next day, Govardhana Puja is performed on that following day - on Pratipada joined with Dvitiya. The text states that when a complete Pratipada carries over to the following day, the rite is to be performed on that following day.

The book notes that some persons, disregarding these clear instructions, employ other verses about go-puja and play with the cows to assign Govardhana Puja to a contaminated Pratipada. The conclusion of the discussion is:

- when the Moon can be seen during Pratipada, go-puja and play with the cows are performed on the preceding day;
- Govardhana Puja itself is performed on the day of Pratipada;
- if because of ksaya-tithi Pratipada appears only together with Dvitiya, Govardhana Puja is performed on that day;
- it is not to be performed on a Pratipada joined with Amavasya.

The book notes that Prabhupada Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Goswami Thakur discussed this issue in detail in the weekly **Gaudiya**, volume 12, issue 11.

---

# Scan 5 - Printed page 9

## Mahadvadashi

There are eight Mahadvadashis.

Four depend on combinations of tithis:

1. Unmilani;
2. Vyanjuli *(Bengali text: “বঞ্জুলী”; the exact Sanskrit form of the name requires verification)*;
3. Trisprisa;
4. Paksavardhini.

Four depend on conjunctions with nakshatras:

1. Jaya;
2. Vijaya;
3. Jayanti;
4. Papanasini.

### Unmilani Mahadvadashi

When a complete Ekadashi is extended and touches the morning of the following day, the Dvadashi of the following day is called **Unmilani Mahadvadashi**.

### Vyanjuli Mahadvadashi

When Ekadashi is complete and Dvadashi is also complete and extended, carrying into Trayodashi, that complete Dvadashi is called **Vyanjuli Mahadvadashi**.

### Trisprisa Mahadvadashi

A day in which Ekadashi, Dvadashi and, at the end of the night, Trayodashi meet is called **Trisprisa Mahadvadashi**.

### Paksavardhini Mahadvadashi

When Amavasya or Purnima is extended, the Dvadashi following the pure Ekadashi that precedes it is called **Paksavardhini Mahadvadashi**.

### The four nakshatra Mahadvadashis

A pure Dvadashi is called:

- **Jaya** when joined with Punarvasu;
- **Vijaya** when joined with Sravana;
- **Jayanti** when joined with Rohini;
- **Papanasini** when joined with Pushya.

Many people are confused about precisely what kind of conjunction produces such a Mahadvadashi. The rule is stated as follows.

If one of the four nakshatras is already operating at sunrise on a day of pure Dvadashi, the day is Mahadvadashi regardless of how much longer the nakshatra continues.

If the nakshatra began before sunrise, it must continue through the entire day and night of Dvadashi or longer. If it continues for less than a full day and night, Mahadvadashi does not arise.

### Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa 13.287 - meaning of the verse

> If the nakshatra began before sunrise and continues longer than a full day and night, or for exactly that length, that day is suitable for observing the vrata.

The book emphasises the word **"equal"**. A full day and night consist of sixty dandas; such a period is called complete, equal, or **sama**.

Ekadashi has a special feature: it is considered complete when it continues for sixty-four dandas, from the preceding Arunodaya until the sunrise following the next Arunodaya.

For a nakshatra Mahadvadashi the following additional conditions are to be considered:

- in conjunction with Punarvasu, Rohini or Pushya, Dvadashi must continue at least until sunset;
- in conjunction with Sravana, for Vijaya Mahadvadashi it is sufficient that Dvadashi continue until one and a half prahar of the day.

---

# Verification notes

1. The translation was made directly from the scan after rotating and enlarging the pages; machine recognition was used only as an auxiliary draft.
2. The main prose text is legible with confidence.
3. The Sanskrit verses are printed in Bengali script. Their English meaning is given here, not a critical edition of the Sanskrit text.
4. The following require additional comparison with the original edition or a Sanskrit source:
   - the decorative line above the name of Srila Bhaktisiddhanta on the cover;
   - the editor's name and several compound calendar names;
   - the exact form “Vyanjuli/Banjuli” Mahadvadashi;
   - the literal syntax of one poetic line about Mayapur and the Ganga.

# Continuation of the translation - printed pages 10-20

## Printed pages 10-11. Instructions concerning the Holy Name

> One should be humbler than grass, more tolerant than a tree, seek no honour for oneself and offer honour to others. In such a state one can constantly chant the name of Hari.

> In this age there is no other way, no other way, no other way than the Holy Name, the Holy Name, the Holy Name of the Lord.

The book emphasises that among the nine limbs of bhakti, **nama-sankirtana** is supreme. When the Holy Name is chanted without offences, one obtains the treasure of prema.

The maha-mantra:

> Hare Krishna, Hare Krishna, Krishna Krishna, Hare Hare;  
> Hare Rama, Hare Rama, Rama Rama, Hare Hare.

It is to be chanted both with a fixed number of repetitions and without limiting the number. The maha-mantra is not intended only for japa; it should also be sung aloud. For the practitioner, kirtana is more merciful than japa.

A fixed number of repetitions helps develop taste for the Name and gradually increase one's daily practice. At the same time, sadhu, sastra and the words of Sri Guru prescribe continuous chanting of countless Names - while eating, sleeping and waking, in happiness and distress. The claim that the maha-mantra cannot be repeated or sung when counting is impossible is not accepted by those learned in bhajana.

> Live at home or in the forest - always call the name of Hari.  
> Do not forget Him in happiness or distress;  
> constantly utter Harinama.

### Pancharatrika diksha and spiritual brahmanhood

In Kali-yuga, the age of quarrel and disagreement, hereditary status alone is insufficient for spiritual purity. Purification is attained through pancharatrika-vidhi and initiation.

Meaning of the cited verse from Sri Hari-bhakti-vilasa:

> Just as bell metal is transformed into gold by a special alchemical process, a person obtains the status of twice-born through proper diksha.

Thus pancharatrika diksha is open to a person irrespective of birth and confers the spiritual brahmanical status needed for service to Bhagavan.

## Printed pages 12-13. Offences to the Holy Name, service and the holy dhama

### Three conditions of uttering the Name

The Name uttered with offences is called **nama-aparadha**. Unintentional offences may yield limited pious results and material happiness; intentional offences lead to severe consequences.

The Name uttered without hostile offence, but not yet with full realisation and pure devotion, is called **namabhasa**, a reflection of the Holy Name. Even namabhasa frees a person from material conditioning.

The Holy Name uttered without offences, with faith, surrender and service, is called **suddha-nama**, the pure Name.

### The ten nama-aparadhas

1. To criticise sadhus and Vaishnavas.
2. To regard Siva and other devas as independent of the Supreme Lord, or as separate supreme rulers equal to Him.
3. To disobey Sri Gurudeva or consider him an ordinary human being.
4. To criticise the Vedas and sastras that glorify the Holy Name.
5. To consider the glorification of the power of the Holy Name an exaggeration.
6. To impose fabricated or worldly interpretations on the Holy Name.
7. To sin deliberately, expecting afterwards to become purified by chanting the Name.
8. To consider chanting the Holy Name one ordinary pious rite, equal to karma, vratas, sacrifices and other worldly merits.
9. To instruct a faithless person who is unwilling to hear about the glory of the Name.
10. Even after hearing the glory of the Name, to maintain indifference, unbelief and attachment to the bodily ideas of “I” and “mine.”

*On the scan, items 8-10 partly merge because of the quality of the printing. The formulations above convey the legible meaning and agree with the standard Gaudiya Vaishnava list of the ten nama-aparadhas; this is not a literal word-for-word transcription of the damaged line.*

### The thirty-two seva-aparadhas

1. To approach the temple in a vehicle or enter wearing shoes.
2. Not to observe the Lord's appearance festivals and other established celebrations.
3. Not to bow before the Deity.
4. To worship in an impure condition or after eating without purification.
5. To bow with one hand.
6. To circumambulate someone else before the Deity instead of properly circumambulating the Deity.
7. To stretch one's legs before the Deity.
8. To sit before the Deity clasping one's knees with the hands.
9. To lie down before the Deity.
10. To eat before the Deity.
11. To speak falsehood before the Deity.
12. To speak too loudly.
13. To engage in worldly conversation.
14. To cry for worldly reasons.
15. To quarrel.
16. To punish or humiliate someone before the Deity.
17. To grant someone worldly patronage before the Deity.
18. To address others with cruel words.
19. To perform service while wrapped in a blanket or coarse covering.
20. To criticise others before the Deity.
21. To glorify ordinary people before the Deity.
22. To utter obscene words.
23. To pass intestinal gas before the Deity.
24. To offer meagre worship although one has the means for complete service.
25. To eat food that has not been offered to the Deity.
26. Not to offer the first seasonal fruits, grains and other new produce.
27. To give the best to others and offer the remainder to the Deity.
28. To sit with one's back to the Deity.
29. To greet other people before the Deity as though they were a more important object of attention.
30. To remain silent in the presence of Sri Guru and not offer him proper prayers and praise.
31. To praise oneself before Sri Guru.
32. To criticise the devas.

### The ten dhama-aparadhas

1. To disregard Sri Guru and the sadhus who reveal the holy dhama.
2. To consider the dhama temporary or material.
3. To envy the residents of the dhama and pilgrims, or judge them by birth and caste.
4. To use residence in the dhama chiefly for income and material gain.
5. To consider the dhama ordinary land, compare its material dimensions and properties with worldly territories, or regard it as equal to ordinary tirthas.
6. To sin in the hope that residence in the dhama will automatically destroy everything.
7. To perceive a spiritual difference between Sri Navadvipa and Sri Vrindavana.
8. To criticise the sastras that glorify the dhama.
9. To disbelieve the glory of the dhama.
10. To regard its glorification as exaggeration or worldly poetic convention.

*One number is omitted typographically in the scan; the semantic list contains ten items.*

### Amrita-yoga and beginning a journey

The book states that the inauspiciousness of Bisti, Vyatipata, papa-yogas, vara-bela and kala-bela is dispelled by the light of Amrita-yoga, just as sunlight destroys darkness. A journey begun in Amrita-yoga brings the desired and auspicious result.

Before departure one is advised to remember the lotus feet of Sri Nrisimhadeva, who removes obstacles, and to see auspicious signs: a cow with her calf, a bull, an elephant, a horse, a flame bending to the right, a virtuous married woman, a brahmana, a Vaishnava, a king, a festively adorned woman, a flower garland, a banner, ghee, yoghurt, honey, silver, gold and clean grain.

## Printed pages 14-20. Introduction to Sri Navadvipa-dhama

The almighty Sri Bhagavan manifests Sri Navadvipa-dhama in the material world through His sandhini-sakti. The true nature of the dhama, beyond the material manifestation, is revealed to consciousness turned toward service.

Sri Navadvipa-dhama is nondifferent from Sri Vrindavana. Its circumference is sixteen krosas. Four islands lie on the eastern bank of the main channel of the Ganga and five on the western bank. These nine islands embody the nine limbs of bhakti: atma-nivedana, sravana, kirtana, smarana, pada-sevana, archana, vandana, dasya and sakhya.

### 1. Antardvipa - atma-nivedana

Sri Yogapitha is situated in Sridham Mayapur - the house of Sri Jagannatha Misra and the appearance place of Sri Gaura, Gaura-janma-bhita. An ancient Tulasi grove and the neem tree that recalls the appearance of Nimai are present here.

Sri Gaura-Narayana is served in the temple at the foot of the neem tree. Other chambers house Sri Pancha-tattva, Sri Jagannathadeva, the vijaya-vigraha of Sri Mahaprabhu and a Deity of Vishnu.

About two hundred yards north of Yogapitha is **Srivasa Angan**, the place of Sri Gaurasundara's great sankirtana with His associates, corresponding to the rasa-sthali in Vrindavana. The temple presents:

1. Sri Gaura-Nityananda performing sankirtana with the devotees;
2. Sri Pancha-tattva and Mahaprabhu's maha-prakasa-lila;
3. Sri Sri Radha-Govinda.

About twenty yards to the north is **Advaita Bhavan**, the residence of Sri Sitanatha Advaita Acharya. Here Advaita Acharya worshipped Sri Krishna with Ganga water and Tulasi leaves according to pancharatrika-vidhi and called Sri Gaura-Krishna to appear in this world.

About ten yards to the east is **Gadadhara Angan**, the house of Madhava Misra, where darsan of Sri Gaura-Gadadhara is performed.

Nearby is the ancient lake of King Ballala Sena, **Ballala-dighi**, formerly called Prithu-kunda.

North of it stands the house of Chandrasekhara Acharya, now **Sri Chaitanya Math**. Here Sri Gaurasundara first arranged a dramatic presentation of Vraja-lila. The Math presents the acharyas of the four Vaishnava sampradayas together with their Deities. It also contains the samadhi mandir of Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Goswami Thakur and the samadhi of his Gurudeva, Srila Gaurakisora Dasa Babaji Maharaj.

The book mentions Isodyana, described in Navadvipa-bhava-taranga, and the publishing service begun by Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati near Sri Radha-kunda at Sri Chaitanya Math. Many books on suddha-bhakti and the periodical Gaudiya were distributed from this principal Math.

Sri Sri Sita-Rama and Narayana are served in the house of Gaura's associate **Jala Murari**.

The following places are also identified:

- Sri Gaura's own ghat, about six yards north of Siva-ghat;
- Madhai-ghat, about thirty yards north of Mahaprabhu's ghat;
- Barakona-ghat, made by Visvakarma, about ten yards north of Madhai-ghat;
- Sridhara Angan, the resting place of Sri Gaurahari during kirtana;
- a samadhi connected with Kamsa of Krishna-lila, whom Mahaprabhu jokingly called His maternal uncle; an ancient Goloka-champa tree grows above it;
- Ballala-dhipi, the remains of King Ballala Sena's palace.

### 2. Simantadvipa - sravana

Here Parvati Devi, a partial manifestation of Srimati Radhika, understood the glory of Sri Gaura and received the happiness of beholding His feet. She placed the dust of Gaura's feet upon the parting of her hair - the **simanta** - and therefore the wise named the island Simantadvipa.

In ordinary speech the locality is called Simuliya. Bilva-puskarini, or the village of Belpukur, and Saradanga belong to this island. The merciful Sri Jagannathadeva resides here to bless the living beings.

### 3. Godrumadvipa - kirtana

In common speech the island is called Gadigacha. Here Surabhi cow bestowed mercy upon Markandeya Muni, who received instruction in Gaura-bhajana and took shelter of pure bhakti. In Krishna-lila this muni had been Indra, who sent the deluge upon Vraja.

**Surabhi-kunja**, established by Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur, is here; the locality is known as Svarupganj. His **Svananda-sukhada-kunja** is nearby. The samadhis of Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur, Srila Gaurakisora Dasa Babaji and his dear servant Sripada Krishnadasa Babaji Maharaj are here.

Sri Gaura-Gadadhara, Sri Radha-Govinda and Siva, the ksetra-pala of the dhama, are continuously served here. The servants of Sri Chaitanya Math continue the worship of the Deities of Sri Gaura-Gadadhara manifested by Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur. Remains of the palace of King Suvarna Sena of Satya-yuga are also preserved on the island.

Siva together with Gauri performs bhajana of Sri Gauranga here, and at the moment of a living being's departure he utters Gaura-nama into that person's ear.

**Sri Nrisimha-palli**, or Deva-palli, is commonly called De-para. After destroying Hiranyakasipu and bestowing mercy upon Prahlada in Satya-yuga, Sri Nrisimhadeva rested here.

### 4. Madhyadvipa - smarana

In common speech the island is called Majida. The bhajana places of the seven rsis are here. South of them is a lake beside which the rsis heard Gaura-bhagavata.

Panchanana Siva left his bull, assumed the form of Hamsa-vahana and, together with the sages, heard narrations of Gaura's qualities. This occurred at midday when the sun stood at the zenith; this explains the name Madhyadvipa.

The island includes **Brahmana-puskara**, also called Bhamana-pukhuri or Bhamana-pura, and **Ucchahatta**, or Hat-danga, which is identical with Kuruksetra. The devas appeared to hold a market here: they gathered and loudly discussed Gaura-katha, giving rise to the name Ucchahatta.

### 5. Koladvipa, or Kuliya - pada-sevana

This is the modern town of Navadvipa on the western bank of the Ganga. Kuliya is known as the place where offences are destroyed. Here Sri Mahaprabhu freed the brahmana Chapala Gopala, who had offended Srivasa Pandita, and Devananda Pandita, who had offended Srimad-Bhagavatam and the devotees, from the consequences of their offences.

The place is known as **Kuliya-pahada**. In Satya-yuga Sri Varahadeva, pleased by the sadhana of the brahmana Vasudeva, appeared here in the gigantic mountain-like form of Varaha.

The bhajana place and samadhi of Vaishnava-sarvabhauma Srila Jagannatha Dasa Babaji Maharaj are here, as is the bhajana place of Srila Vamsidasa Babaji Maharaj.

### 6. Ritudvipa - archana

The villages Champahatta, or Tapahati, and other localities belong to the island. In the past there was a forest of champaka trees here, and flowers were sold in abundance at a market for worship of the Deities; the place therefore became known as Champahatta. It corresponds to Khadiravana, one of the twelve forests of Vrindavana.

Sakhi Champakalata weaves garlands of champaka flowers here and serves Sri Radha-Krishna.

The Deities of Sri Gaura-Gadadhara worshipped by Gaura's associate Dvija Vaninatha have been here for more than four hundred years. The place is now known as **Sri Gaura-Gadadhara Math**, and the Deities are served daily by devotees of Sri Chaitanya Math.

The six seasons headed by spring worshipped Sri Gaura Bhagavan here while meditating upon His avatara; the island is therefore called Ritudvipa.

Here the poet Sri Jayadeva Thakur, author of Gita-Govinda, and Padmavati Devi served Sri Radha-Krishna with garlands of champaka flowers in the mood of raga-marga. Bhagavan Sri Krishna granted them His darsan. Here the ocean took shelter of the Ganga and beheld Navadvipa-lila; the place is regarded as Gangasagara-tirtha itself.

### 7. Jahnudvipa - vandana

In common speech the island is called Jannagara. It corresponds to Bhadravana, one of the twelve forests of Vraja-mandala. Here Jahnu Muni received darsan of Sri Gaurasundara and attained perfection in his tapasya.

**Vidyanagara** is the abode of all branches of knowledge. Rsis of every age were educated here: Valmiki received inspiration to compose poetry; Narada and other rsis, to expound Pancharatra; Vyasa and other sages, to compile the Puranas. The Srutis worshipped Sri Gaura here.

Deva-guru Brihaspati appeared in Gaura-lila as Vasudeva Sarvabhauma, founded a school here and, by the mercy of Sri Gaurasundara, abandoned enjoyment of external scholarship and took shelter of the highest knowledge, suddha-bhakti.

### 8. Modadrumadvipa - dasya

During Rama-lila, Bhagavan lived here in a hut beneath a great banyan tree while in forest exile. Seeing this place increases the joy of service, and therefore it is called Modadrumadvipa. It corresponds to Bhandiravana in Vrindavana.

The village **Mamgachi** is on the island - the appearance place and childhood playground of Srila Vrindavana Dasa Thakur, the Vyasa of Chaitanya-lila and author of Sri Chaitanya-bhagavata. His Vyasa-pitha, surrounded by trees, reminds devotees of sacred Naimisaranya and is called the “Naimisa of Gauda.” The parental home of Malini Devi, the wife of Srivasa Pandita, was here.

Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Goswami Thakur established **Modadruma Gaudiya Math** here and entrusted it with the service of the Deities of Sri Gaura-Nityananda worshipped by Vrindavana Dasa Thakur. Sri Sri Radha-Madana-Gopala, installed by Vasudeva Datta Thakur, and Sri Sri Radha-Gopinatha, installed by Gaura's associate Saranga Murari, also reside here.

Part of the island is called **Mahatpura**, or Matapura, because the five Pandavas lived here incognito for some time. The book specifically notes that the name “Madhaipura” is a later mistake. Vaikuntha-pitha, or Narayanapura, is also situated on Modadrumadvipa.

### 9. Rudradvipa - sakhya

Here the eleven Rudras headed by Nilalohita worshipped Sri Gaura. Kailasa-dhama is only a reflection of Rudradvipa's radiance.

Astvakra, Dattatreya and other yogis abandoned here the offensive idea of an impersonal nondual Absolute and concentrated upon the lotus feet of Sri Krishna Chaitanya.

Here the acharya Vishnusvami, teacher of suddhadvaita-vada, received mercy and became the founder of his sampradaya. Here the mercy of Gaura invisibly entered the heart of Sridhara Svami, by which he interpreted Srimad-Bhagavatam in the spirit of suddhadvaita and became dear to Sri Gaurasundara.

At present this island lies on the eastern bank of the Ganga. Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Goswami Thakur established **Sri Rudradvipa Gaudiya Math** here.

The caption beneath the image of the Deities reads: **“Sri Sri Guru-Gauranga-Gandharvika-Giridhari Jiu.”**

# Final accuracy assessment

- Printed pages 2-20 were translated with manual checking against the scans.
- The calendar contains all 385 civil dates from 4 March 2026 through 23 March 2027 without omissions.
- The entries for 15-18 and 29-30 June 2026 were rechecked directly against the original Bengali scans and corrected in this revision.
- The remaining calendar entries were structured automatically from enhanced OCR. The symbol `≈` marks a reconstructed time digit; unreadable passages are not presented as exact.
- The printed panjika does not provide a complete description of the astronomical model used to calculate tithi. Its times should be stored as source data, separately from modern geocentric ephemerides.
- For astronomical calculation, determination of parana and religious practice, every entry not marked as rechecked must be compared with the original Bengali scan.
- The last two printed pages of the source file are nearly blank.
